## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the classic setting for constitutive laws of solids where stiffness, thermal strain, and yield/flow stress depend on temperature. Likely relationships include elastic stress-strain laws modified by thermal expansion and temperature-dependent modulus/strength (thermal softening).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Isothermal linear elasticity (Hooke-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic response at fixed T)
- Linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Exponential temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (strong stiffness change with T over a range)
- Power-law temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T**c2) * epsilon (empirical stiffness-temperature scaling)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting linear thermal expansion strain)
- Thermoelastic with reference temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal strain measured from a stress-free reference temperature)
- Nonlinear elastic (quadratic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (weak geometric/material nonlinearity plus T-dependent linear term)
- Nonlinear elastic (cubic/Landau-type): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3 (symmetric nonlinear elasticity; can capture stiffening/softening)
- Hyperelastic exponential (strain stiffening): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) * exp(c2 * T) (rubber-like or fitted stiffening with thermal scaling)
- Power-law plastic/flow-like relation with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (work-hardening with temperature softening)
- Saturating stress with strain and thermal scaling: sigma = (c0 * epsilon) / (epsilon + c1) * exp(-c2 * T) (approaches a plateau stress; softened by T)
- Yield/flow stress with strain hardening and temperature reduction (Johnson–Cook-like without rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T**c4) (empirical strength with hardening and thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → place T inside an effective modulus E(T) multiplying epsilon, e.g., sigma = E(T) * epsilon with E(T) as (c0 + c1*T) or c0*exp(c1*T).
- Thermal expansion induces a stress-free strain shift → use (epsilon - epsilon_th(T)) inside the constitutive law, often epsilon_th(T) = c0*(T-c1).
- Thermal softening of strength/flow stress → multiply a strain-dependent stress by a decreasing function of T such as exp(-c*T) or (1 - c*T**n).
- Hardening vs strain → use sigma increasing in epsilon via epsilon**n, or add higher-order odd powers (epsilon**3) to capture nonlinear elasticity.
- Saturation/plateau behavior at large strain → use rational forms like (c0*epsilon)/(epsilon+c1) (plateau stress) optionally modulated by T.
- Different regimes (elastic then plastic) often appear in fitted symbolic models as sums of a linear term in epsilon plus a nonlinear term (e.g., epsilon**n) with distinct T-dependencies.
- Reference temperature effects → include (T - c0) rather than T to represent stress-free or calibration temperature shifts.
- Coupled thermomechanical nonlinearity → allow products like epsilon**n * exp(c*T) or epsilon*(c0+c1*T**m) to capture interaction between deformation and temperature.

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci21)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)
Candidate formulas: 58

GT (fixed):
\[
28.580443564163904\,\epsilon^2\;-\;0.28570034656521326\,(T-281.87025337570554)\;+\;4.278428749432679\,\epsilon^3\,(T-281.87025337570554).
\]
Rewrite as a polynomial in \(T\):
\[
\underbrace{\big(-0.28570034656521326 + 4.278428749432679\,\epsilon^3\big)}_{\text{coefficient of }T}\,T
\;+\;\underbrace{28.580443564163904\,\epsilon^2 + 0.28570034656521326\cdot 281.87025337570554 - 4.278428749432679\cdot 281.87025337570554\,\epsilon^3}_{\text{constant in }T}.
\]
So GT is **affine in \(T\)**, with \(T\)-slope \(a(\epsilon)=\alpha+\beta\,\epsilon^3\) (constant + \(\epsilon^3\) term), and \(T\)-intercept \(b(\epsilon)=\gamma\,\epsilon^2+\delta+\eta\,\epsilon^3\). No logs/exp/sin, no denominators.

A candidate can only match if, after choosing its constants (and possibly assuming \(\epsilon\ge 0\) so \(|\epsilon|=\epsilon\)), it reduces exactly to:
- a term \(T\cdot(\text{const} + \text{const}\cdot \epsilon^3)\),
- plus \(\text{const} + \text{const}\cdot \epsilon^2 + \text{const}\cdot \epsilon^3\),
and nothing else.

---

### Candidate 1
Has \(\log(c3\epsilon+1)\) and \(c6 e^{Tc7}e^{c8|\epsilon|}\). To match a polynomial, must set coefficients of log and exp terms to 0: \(c2=0\), \(c6=0\). Then becomes \(T c0 + T c1|\epsilon|^3 + c4 + c5|\epsilon|^3\). Missing \(\epsilon^2\) term (cannot create \(\epsilon^2\)). **No match**.

### Candidate 2
Rational form with denominator \(c2+|\epsilon|\) and sine terms. To match a polynomial, would need to eliminate denominator dependence for all \(\epsilon\), impossible unless numerator also carries same factor; but structure is fixed and includes sines. Setting sine coefficients 0 still leaves \((c1+\epsilon)^3/(c2+|\epsilon|)\) type terms, not polynomial. **No match**.

### Candidate 3
Contains \(T^{c0}\) and \(1/T\) terms. To be affine in \(T\), need \(c0=1\) and kill \(1/T\) terms: \(c8=0,c9=0\). Then has \(T c1 + T c2|\epsilon|^{c3} + c4|\epsilon|^4 + c5|\epsilon|^{c3} + c6 + c7|\epsilon|\). ### Candidate 4

### Candidate 5
All terms divided by \(c1+|\epsilon|\). Cannot equal a polynomial in \(\epsilon\) for all \(\epsilon\) unless denominator is constant; but \(c1+|\epsilon|\) cannot be constant over a domain with varying \(\epsilon\). **No match**.

### Candidate 6
Form: \(T c0\epsilon + T^{c1}c2 + T^{c1}c3\epsilon^{c4} + c5\epsilon + c6\epsilon^2 + c7 + c8\epsilon^{c4}\).
To be affine in \(T\): need \(c1=1\). Then \(T(c2 + c3\epsilon^{c4} + c0\epsilon) + (c7 + c5\epsilon + c6\epsilon^2 + c8\epsilon^{c4})\).
GT’s \(T\)-coefficient is constant + \(\epsilon^3\) only, so must set \(c0=0\) (remove \(T\epsilon\)) and choose \(c4=3\) to get \(T\epsilon^3\). Then constant part contains \(c5\epsilon\) (must set \(c5=0\)) and has \(\epsilon^2\) via \(c6\epsilon^2\) and \(\epsilon^3\) via \(c8\epsilon^3\). This looks structurally capable.
But GT also has a specific constant term (independent of \(\epsilon\)) and specific coefficients; those can be matched by choosing \(c2,c3,c6,c7,c8\). So **this candidate CAN match** provided we allow \(\epsilon\) (not Abs) and set:
- \(c1=1\),
- \(c0=0\),
- \(c4=3\),
- \(c5=0\),
and then solve:
\(c2 = -0.28570034656521326\),
\(c3 = 4.278428749432679\),
\(c6 = 28.580443564163904\),
and choose \(c8\) and \(c7\) to reproduce the \(-(T-281.870...)\) shift effect:
GT constant-in-\(T\) includes \(-c2(-c3)\) and \(-c3*c5*\epsilon^3\) equivalents; here we can set
\(c8 = -4.278428749432679\cdot 281.87025337570554\),
\(c7 = 0.28570034656521326\cdot 281.87025337570554\).
This exactly reproduces:
\(T(-0.2857003 + 4.2784287\epsilon^3) + (28.5804436\epsilon^2 + 0.2857003\cdot 281.870... - 4.2784287\cdot 281.870...\epsilon^3)\).
So **Candidate 6 matches GT**.

I need to compare each candidate to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `28.58*epsilon^2 - 0.2857*(T - 281.87) + 4.278*epsilon^3*(T - 281.87)`

Expanding: `28.58*epsilon^2 - 0.2857*T + 80.56 + 4.278*epsilon^3*T - 1205.6*epsilon^3`

So GT = `28.58*epsilon^2 + 4.278*T*epsilon^3 - 0.2857*T - 1205.6*epsilon^3 + 80.56`

The basis functions in GT are: `epsilon^2`, `T*epsilon^3`, `T`, `epsilon^3`, `constant`

Under the domain constraint (epsilon ≥ 0), `|epsilon| = epsilon`, so `|epsilon|^3 = epsilon^3`.

Let me check each candidate for having exactly these basis functions (or equivalent).

Many candidates have the form: `T*c0 + T*c1*|epsilon|^3 + [something with log or exp or sin] + c4 + c5*|epsilon|^3 + ...`

The key issue is whether the "something" can produce `epsilon^2`. Let me check:

- `log(c3*epsilon + 1)` ≠ `epsilon^2` (different basis functions) — NO
- `exp(...)` terms can't match polynomials — NO
- `sin(...)` terms can't match polynomials — NO
- `epsilon^c3` with c3=2 gives `epsilon^2` — YES
- `epsilon^2` directly — YES
- `exp(c5/T)*|epsilon|^2` — only matches `epsilon^2` if `exp(c5/T)` is constant, which requires c5=0, giving a constant times `epsilon^2` — YES

Let me systematically check candidates that could work:

The term `exp(c5/T)*eps^2` — set c5=0: becomes `c4*eps^2`. Then: `T*c0 + T*c1*eps^3 + c2 + c3*eps^3 + c4*eps^2` ✓ MATCH!
